You'd have to stop the world

by Echolux

Summary

In the events leading up to Jen and Alice’s wedding, their respective best friends Agatha and Rio have to work together despite their… creative differences.

Oh, and then there’s this:
Rio doesn’t fall for straight women. Agatha's not a lesbian. And one of them is lying.

Notes

Hello! I’m usually more of a dramatic writer but the world is on fire so I’m trying my hands on something more fun. I’m borrowing Marvel’s characters and inspiration from Chappell Roan’s ‘Good luck, Babe’ to do so (like many people here have found the power in MarvelxChappell and I LOVE it).

Just a heads up: I can’t write a coherent story without a little drama so there will be some angst caused by internalized homophobia, and actions/behaviors because of it. Happy ending guaranteed because - lesbians.

it's fine, it's cool

It isn’t that Agatha wouldn’t rather spend her Saturday evening on her sofa – legs sprawled out in front of her, a glass of red in her right hand, TV remote in her left; watching some rerun of a show she’s already seen a hundred times, occasionally looking out the window to judge the neighbors for their meticulously kept lawn, because how dare they, and making a mental note to really, actually, no excuses this time, mow her own lawn. Next week. Maybe.

No, that’s not it. It’s also not that she has a profound passion for commercialized unnecessary festivities like an engagement party. When her friend Jen had shown her the ring, Agatha had really tried to understand- she'd searched thoroughly, checked every corner of her brain to find a reason to celebrate the fact someone was about to do something in the future, that would ultimately also require a celebration… But had found none.
And while she does believe that Jen and her fiancée Alice are deeply in love with each other, because they clearly are – taking every little step in their relationship as an excuse to throw a party like this is just… too much . It’s the first of many to come, she knows: two bachelorette parties, a rehearsal, a pre-wedding and the actual wedding are in her near future. She prays to whoever will listen that Jen and Alice aren’t planning on having a baby soon, as she can only imagine how many heinous parties will be a part of that process.

So, what is it then? Why is she here?
Must be friendship or something, she guesses, a disgusted look on her face as she plucks a pink ‘ she said yes !’ skewer from a donut and tosses it aside. Or the open bar.

“Please keep reminding me to never, never, ever, get married.” Right as Agatha is about to take a bite, Jen snatches the donut away from her.

"Leave it! The party doesn’t start for another hour,” Jen hisses. Before she can put the donut back on the tray, Agatha grabs her by the wrist and takes a bite anyway, which causes for a (well deserved, sure ) eye roll.

“Who else is coming? Anyone I know?” Agatha inquires, mouth full of donut. Jen sighs, admitting defeat, and surrenders the baked good.

“Wanda and the twins are gonna be there,” she says, knowing that will piss Agatha off. Indeed it does, which she emphasizes with a very vocal “ugh” .

“Then there’s Lilia, Monica, Mr. and Mrs. Hart, the Proctors…”

Jen counts them on her fingers. Agatha lets out an even bigger “ugh” .

“And you remember Rio?”

“Double ugh , is that the one who can’t stop flirting with me?” Agatha asks, raking a hand through her unruly brown locks as she takes another bite. She knows, of course she knows who Rio is. Alice’s friend; an athletic, yet elegant lady with dark hair and tanned skin, some latina in there, maybe?, big brown puppy eyes, and a very frustrating sense of confidence that she uses to try and woo Agatha at every chance she gets.

The last time they had all gone out together, Agatha had been too drunk to realize Rio was just playing with her when she repeatedly gestured at her lips, as if to say Agatha had something in the corner of her mouth. Agatha had rubbed her cheek a few times, her fingers coming back clean every time, and had silently gestured for Rio to do it for her. Only when Rio had shuffled closer, closer, into her personal space, a smug look on her face, raising a hand– she noticed Jen and Alice in her peripheral vision on the other side of the booth, hands covering their mouths to not laugh out loud. It had earned Rio some physical contact alright, but not the kind she’d hoped for. A smack upside the head, “oh for fuck’s sake!”, a shove, “ stay out of my aura!”, and a series of swats against her arm every time she so much as thought about looking in Agatha’s general direction.
Oh, she knows Rio.

“You’re making that up,” Jen deadpans. Agatha lets her jaw drop, giving Jen an unpleasant view of whatever is left of the donut in her mouth. “Ha-ha, now please close your mouth and keep folding the napkins.” Jen gets up and turns around, completely oblivious to the bird Agatha flips her.

“Sure thing, hon!” Agatha says in a saccharine voice, but as soon as Jen is far away enough, her smile drops and she tosses the napkins aside carelessly.



And as the evening progresses and guests start showing up, music’s playing, people chatting, children dancing, Agatha does absolutely nothing to hide the fact that she’s bored out of her skull. No one can blame her, really, when she’s forced to resort to her favorite pastime. The cheap merlot across the room will have to do.

The rest of the night could have been fairly uneventful too, if it wasn’t for Agatha tripping over a bunch of pink and silver balloons on her way to the bar.

Swearing loudly, she tries to break free from the strings, which only causes her to get even more tangled up. She swears again, and sees Wanda scowling at her from the corner of her eye. Inhaling deeply to come up with even more creative profanities, she’s interrupted by Jen who jumps in and covers her mouth with her hand.

“Oh for the love of–  Agatha, there are children here,” she says, her voice as stern as her gaze.

“Yeah, well, they have to learn at some point, don’t they?” Agatha huffs when Jen lowers her hand. Still fighting the balloon strings that are wrapped around her ankle, she casts another glance at Wanda, who is desperately trying to distract one of the twins.

“I’d say there’s no one better to learn that kind of language from than you,” Jen’s fiancée pipes up. She chuckles, sliding her arm around Jen’s waist. “Hi, Agatha.”

Agatha presses her heel into one of the balloons and it explodes with a loud BANG , accidentally drawing a lot of attention to herself. She squints at Alice, who looks like she’s about to brace for impact.

“You,” she says, pointing at her, “I always knew I liked you. You’re approved. One of Jen’s best characteristics seems to be her taste in other people.”
She turns her pointed finger towards herself and gestures down her own body, clad in a white blouse and purple slacks. “Meaning myself, mostly.”

“Oh, and I bet one of your best traits is being humble?” Jen sneers, which causes a third person to snicker. Agatha’s eyes whip up from her own legs to the person now standing next to Alice. She recognizes Rio, dressed in a tailored black suit and matching pumps.

“What are you laughing at?” Agatha barks, sounding slightly less hostile than she wants to.

”Oh, you remember Rio, right?” Alice steps up, nodding towards her friend who is taking Agatha in with an amused smile.

“I’m not sure, have we met?” Rio takes a step forward, holding out her hand for Agatha to shake. Agatha can see in her eyes she knows damn well they’d met. She is being an asshole and Agatha is not going to give her the satisfaction. Or maybe she is.

“Eh,” Agatha shows off her best unimpressed shrug, “I’m not surprised I don’t remember someone who’d show up to an engagement party dressed in all black. My god, who died, dear?”

“Your manners, apparently,” Rio fires back, sounding equally unimpressed. Accepting the fact that Agatha isn’t gonna shake her hand, she slips it right back into her pocket, a little bit too smug for Agatha’s liking. She purses her lips, sends a pointed look in Rio’s direction, and turns to Alice.

“I was just complimenting Jen on her taste in friends, but Alice, dear, don’t take it the wrong way when I say that yours is spectacularly subpar.”

“Alright!” Jen claps her hands loudly to break the tension. “I need wine.”

She turns around to grab two glasses off the bar and hands one to Alice, who gratefully accepts. Rio, being the insufferable show-off that she is, also takes two glasses off the bar and offers one to Agatha. “M’lady?”

Agatha seeks out Jen’s gaze for a millisecond, as to say: ‘ see?’ before reaching out to accept the wine. But as her fingers graze Rio’s, a strong static shock sears through both of them. Agatha gasps and jumps back, as Rio shouts “Ouch!” and promptly drops the glass. It shatters into a million pieces, red wine spilling all over the floor and, oh no, Agatha’s black shoes.

Agatha’s nostrils flare as she looks down, slowly inhaling. Making eye contact with Rio again, she can feel her hands practically turning into claws. A dangerous, almost feral look on her face, she lifts her arms to launch herself at Rio. Just before she can attack her, Jen jumps in between the two of them.

“You!” Agatha growls over Jen’s shoulder. “Look what you did! Do you have ANY idea…”

“Me?” Rio scoffs. “If you hadn’t declared war on some party decorations, we wouldn’t have been electrocuted.” She wiggles her fingers to get rid of the tingling feeling in them, and reaches down to pick up some of the bigger pieces of glass.

“Agatha, bathroom,” Jen says to her friend, desperately wanting to defuse the situation. Agatha exhales, and turns around dramatically.
“Are you gonna tell her she’ll be paying for dry cleaning?” she shouts over her shoulder as she walks away. “And get me another glass of red. Pronto.”



Agatha knows Jen's practically put her in the time-out corner, but at least she feels a little calmer when she returns after a while. She silently slips into a booth in the back of the venue, closes her eyes with a sigh, slumps down, and drops her head against the backrest. The loud music isn’t doing much for her ability to be friendly and social. Just 30 more minutes, she promises herself, then she’s allowed to go home.

With her eyes still closed, she feels a slight dip in the cushion, as someone slides into the booth with her. It better not be–
Cracking one eye open, she lets out an annoyed huff at the sight of Rio.

“Oh please, not you. You lost the right to talk to me today,” she murmurs softly, but loud enough for Rio to hear.

“You sure? I came to make it up to you, sweetheart,” Rio says, putting two intact wine glasses down on the table.

“Don’t call me– oh.” Agatha eyes up the generously poured peace offering in front of her, and shuffles in her seat so she sits upright again. “Well. Fine. You may stay.”

She picks up her glass just as Rio picks up hers. She puts it to her lips right away, ignoring Rio’s invitation to clink their glasses together.

“It’s good to know you can be bribed,” Rio hums softly, before sipping her own drink.

“It’s not bribing if you give me something and I give you nothing in return.”

“And yet, here you are, having a conversation with me, while a moment ago I wasn’t allowed to talk to you,” Rio says, with that smirk on her face.

“Yeah, well, momentary lapse of judgment. I’m revoking that right again, as you can’t seem to stop being annoying,” Agatha shoots back, hoping that is going to be it.

Agatha can’t truthfully say she hates the ego boost she gains from Rio’s flattery, from being clearly found attractive– but Rio isn’t anything if not relentless, arrogant, and above all, a woman. Agatha being Jen’s best friend, she is supportive of the queer community in all the ways, it just isn’t for her. Sure, she’d kissed plenty of her female classmates back in the day, but nothing she’d want to do again.

So as Agatha has nothing to win or lose from Rio, she doesn’t really mind keeping up their playful banter. Some might even call it flirting– but she’d been very clear about being straight, which had seemed to throw Rio off a little at the time. However both women had soon realized their banter keeps them on their toes. It’s innocent and it’s fun .

Agatha catches herself staring at Rio’s face, whose eyes are sparkling at the challenge. Rio raises her eyebrows, looks away, and mimes locking up her lips.
She tears her eyes away from Rio’s mouth, only to land on the three opened buttons of her blouse. Realizing there had only been one unbuttoned earlier, she can’t stop herself from saying: “Wow. You sure ammo’d up.”
Shaking her head, she takes another sip. Rio locks eyes with her again.

“Glad you noticed,” she says, straightening her shoulders, leaning one elbow on the table, chin in hand. “What can I say, I know what I want. Is it working?”

Agatha snorts. “Ha! No. Still not on Team Boobs.”

It’s Rio’s time to shake her head. “Yeah… you’re actually insane for that.”

“Who’s insane?” Jen appears in front of the booth, followed by Alice.

“I am, of course,” Agatha takes a dramatic bow, “for not showing any interest in female genitalia.”

“Well, you’re not making it sound very sexy,” Rio mumbles. Alice takes in the two women before clocking what is going on.

“Down, boy,” she says to Rio, making an ‘I’m watching you’ gesture. “Agatha’s not on our team.” A beat. “But I’m glad the two of you are getting along.”

“Oh, yeah, basically besties,” Agatha drawls, a fake smile on her face.

“When the two of you are done being children, I think it’s time for the speeches,” Jen says. The color drains from Agatha’s face. The goddamn fucking speeches.

“We’ll start,” Jen explains, as she and her fiancée share a mysterious look, “and then we’ll call you on stage. Who wants to go first?”

Agatha feigns a sudden fascination for the edge of the table cloth. She can feel Rio’s eyes on her. “You’re giving a speech too?” Rio muses, and Agatha wonders if it would be too dramatic of an exit to pull the fire alarm and jump through the nearest window.

“Actually…” Agatha sighs. “I would’ve loved to , Jen, and you know it. But I can’t possibly hold a speech with those wine stains all over my shoes.”
And besides, she all but chugged that last glass of wine, so public speaking is definitely not on top of the list of smart things to do right now.

“You’re just being a bitch right now, it’s a red wine stain on black shoes ,” Jen says. “For that, you should be going first. Barefoot if you must.” And before Agatha can protest, Jen and Alice wander off towards the stage.

Agatha looks at Rio, ready to berate her on how she hadn’t stepped in to help, but Rio is hiding her grin behind her glass.

“I can’t wait to see this.”

As soon as Jen and Alice climb the small stage, the music quietens and one of the venue’s techs hands Jen a microphone. The soft murmuring of the guests dies down as she begins talking.

“Welcome everybody! Dear friends, family, acquaintances… My lovely fiancée and I are honored to have you all here, celebrating our engagement.”

The guests applaud as Jen gives Alice a peck on the lips, pulling her in by the waist. A few of the guests start cheering, among them Rio – which causes Agatha to dramatically cover the ear that is closest to her. Rio pouts, then whistles on her fingers, and Agatha gets distracted by a very vivid fantasy about squeezing the other woman’s windpipe until her eyes pop out.

On stage, Alice takes over the mic.

“I hope you’re all enjoying the food and the music, but we’d like to interrupt for just a moment. Agatha and Rio, would you please join us up here?”

Agatha prays for an interruption, anything will do, but nothing happens. The two women exchange a look, and now Agatha can sense Rio isn’t particularly happy about being asked on stage either. Good.
Still, they scramble out of the booth, taking their wine glasses with them. The guests politely applaud once more while they walk to the front. As they approach the stage, Jen helps them up, Rio takes her place on Alice’s side, and Agatha goes to stand next to Jen, where she nervously starts picking some non-existent lint off her slacks.

Alice holds the mic in between herself and Jen, so the both of them can speak.

“So Agatha, Rio… as you know, we asked you to prepare a few words for tonight,” Alice says, looking from one to the other. Rio nervously shuffles her feet as Agatha squints into the stage lights. She hasn’t forgotten, she just prefers… improvising.

“Now, that wasn’t just to torture you,” Jen smirks. “It’s also to prepare you for the big day! Special announcement, drumroll please…  Agatha, I’d like you to be my maid of honor.”

Jen looks at her as if she has just crowned her best friend as emperor, clearly expecting some kind of response. But Agatha’s breath hitches and she stays awkwardly silent, so Alice quickly adds: “And Rio, I’d love for you to be my best man! Eh– Woman. Person. Pick one. Or all of the above.”

The guests start laughing and cheering, as Agatha and Rio find each other’s gaze. Agatha squints, ‘did you know about this?’ but Rio seems just as surprised.

The engaged couple reels their respective friend in by wrapping an arm around their shoulder, pulling them in closer.

“This obviously means you have your work cut out for the both of you,” Jen announces into the mic.

“I hate you,” Agatha says through a big fake smile.

“-...But Alice and I are convinced you’ll get along fine and we’re putting all of our faith in you.”

“Does that mean we don’t actually have to give our speeches?” Agatha whispers.

“Of course it doesn’t mean you don’t actually have to do your speeches!” Alice repeats loudly, much to Agatha’s disdain. “Who’s first?”

Agatha looks over at Rio, who is sucking in her cheek and clearly trying to avoid any eye contact. After a few excruciating seconds of silence, Agatha grabs the mic, only to avoid further humiliation.

“I’ll take one for the team,” she snaps at Rio, taking center stage while the other women shuffle to the back.

Agatha clears her throat and shields her eyes from the harsh lighting, squinting again to oversee the whole floor. Contemplating whether she’d rather stick the microphone up the ass of the first person who looks at her funny, she at least feels a little spurred on by the alcohol in her system.

“Well,” she accidentally yells, voice cracking, clearing her throat once more. “Well. Hello.” She takes a breath and puts her hand on her hip. “Hi.”

“Great start!” she hears someone behind her whisper – must be Rio. The hairs in the back of Agatha’s neck stand up and she makes a mental note to make her windpipe fantasies come true at the first opportunity.

“So eh – Jen and Alice. Alice and… Jen. That’s… these two women over here,” she stutters. “The happy couple.”

The silence in the room is deafening. She turns around to the other women, and wordlessly asks if this was good enough to pass as a speech. She is met with all of them giving her a thumbs up as to say ‘ keep going!’.

Agatha feels something bubbling inside her chest. This isn’t how this is gonna go, public speaking is not going to be the great Agatha Harkness’ demise. And if it is, she sure as hell will take the others with her.

“Alright, I’m assuming everybody here knows that Jen and I have been friends for a million years now. But how about I tell everybody how I met her lovely fiancée Alice over here?”

“Agatha, no,” a voice warns behind her, that she chooses to ignore.

“Jen and I used to be roommates, before these two became inseparable,” she continues. Her newfound vigor causes her to pace the stage.

”We had a few house rules, most of them initiated by Jen of course. But the one she was most adamant about, was ‘ absolutely no boys, Agatha',” she says, mimicking Jen’s low voice. “And I, the amazing friend that I am, never asked her if that same rule applied to her. Because I trusted that she wouldn’t. Our holy virgin mother Mary over here.”

She gracefully points at Jen, who turns an interesting shade of red.

“And I have to admit, even I make mistakes sometimes. Like the one time I’d just been out on a date, a really nice date, he brought me home and– well, we made out in the hallway, I guess. My bad, fair enough. But when the cool, calm, and collected Jenny Kale caught us there, she exploded like an atomic bomb. Gave the both of us a total earful, scared him away, naturally, and I was on the receiving end of a very long monologue about friendship, trust, and boundaries.
Which would be fair, if…”

The couple behind her holds their breath in anticipation. A high whine escapes from Alice’s throat.

“If not for the fact that only a few days later, I come home from work early… And what view am I being blessed with? Oh you guessed it, people! A full blast, uncensored graphic scene, performed by your leading ladies Alice and Jen, in the fucking kitchen nonetheless, making noises like they’re auditioning for the next pornographic feature length! What an incredible day to have eyes. And the worst part: on the counter, in its full glory, is this big, fat, rubber-…”

“Okay that’s enough!” Jen shrieks, trying to grab the mic from Agatha’s hands, who now surprisingly enough doesn’t want to give it up. Guests start murmuring again, and Agatha can just make out Wanda’s silhouette walking out with the twins. Nice.

“But because I’m such a forgiving person, you have my full blessing!” Agatha all but yells in the microphone that she and Jen were now fighting over. “To the happy horny couple!” She raises her glass and finally gives up her iron grip, turns around with flair and crosses paths with Rio.

“Your turn. Eat shit,” she whispers when she accidentally bumps into her shoulder.

“Such sportsmanship,” Rio murmurs from the corner of her mouth.

Agatha takes Rio’s place in the back and crosses her arms with a smirk – she has done pretty well, she thinks. She highly doubts Rio will display any skill or grace, talking to a room full of people like this. Oh, this is gonna be good. Licking her lips, she watches as Rio takes the spotlight.




This is how Agatha learns about the consequences of making unsubstantiated assumptions. Nothing could have prepared her for the mere elegance , the striking confidence that radiates from Rio while she talks. She finds herself completely thunderstruck at Rio’s clearly well-prepared and loving speech for the couple. Clenching her teeth so as not to let her mouth hang open, she follows her every move – from the casual pacing, her laid back posture, to the eloquently chosen words… It is the most stupid and impressive thing Agatha has ever witnessed, and she can only see her from the back.

“…and I mean it with my entire heart when I say: I’m truly honored to be your best man, Al. I’ll wear a bow tie and everything,” Rio chuckles, as she playfully tugs the collar of her blazer. Someone in the back of the room wolf whistles, which makes Rio point at them, treating them to a quick wink. Agatha feels the heat rise to her cheeks.

“Finally, I’d like to add…” Rio continues, holding her hand up as to excuse herself. She turns around to quickly jog towards Agatha, who breaks from her trance when her hand is grabbed and she gets pulled to the front of the stage again. Here we fucking go, she thinks.

“…that both Agatha and I couldn’t possibly think of anyone we’d rather prepare the wedding with, than each other. This,--” she gestures between the both of them, “--is pure wedding material.”

Agatha can feel Rio smirk at her own double entendre. The music gets louder - a sign they should be wrapping up.

Putting on her fake smile again, Agatha snarls: “I’m going to kill you.”

“Oh please, and do it slowly,” Rio’s rasps, careful not to let those words reach the microphone.

If Agatha could lift her up, she would’ve hurled her off the stage.

a new excuse

Chapter Notes

minor trigger warning for the mention of assisted suicide near the end of the chapter
(and if it helps; it's not about the leading ladies)

She would never admit it if you ask her, but Agatha does acknowledge her initial response might’ve been a little dramatic. Being her best friend’s maid of honor is a huge token of appreciation – not because of what it practically entails, but because she knows how much it means to Jen herself.

Jen, the only friend she allows to put her back in place, even if it provokes some lighthearted death threats. Jen, with a personality so completely opposite from her own, it only made sense they grew so close. Jen, who recognizes Agatha’s snarky remarks and numerous eye rolls for what they really are, and always responds accordingly; whether it is with a healthy dose of sarcasm, a bottle of wine and a tissue box, or a 30-minute long voice note (that Agatha had lovingly dubbed ‘Have Mercy, Jen’s Yapping - The Podcast’) with her perspective and opinion on a given situation.
Jen, who had texted her Rio’s number a few days after the engagement party, strongly advising her to give her a call so they could start planning.
Jen, who is now officially going to pay for therapy and her pacemaker.

I’ll send you a to-do list so you know what’s expected of you, Jen texts her when Agatha responds to Rio’s number with an emoji wearing a cowboy hat. She’d meant to click the clown one, but she’s sure this one conveys the message too.

I hope you know what you’re asking, she replies.

Yes. I do.

For the next couple of weeks Agatha does what she does best: procrastinate. It doesn’t help that the wedding isn’t gonna take place for another six months. It also doesn’t help that she apparently has to initiate the call, nor that she doesn’t feel particularly excited about the amount of work she has to put in. It does help however, when Jen starts threatening to give her address to the local Jehovah’s Witness community if she doesn’t get to work soon.



When Agatha finally calls Rio, it’s a Sunday night and she’s in the bath. If Rio pisses her off, she’d figured, she’s already in the right place to relax. That, or she could always throw her phone in the water.

Against the whole world’s expectations, the conversation doesn’t seem to go completely off the rails. It seems – civil, almost. They share their thoughts on how ridiculous it is that their friends had just dumped these duties on them, however Rio seems to be looking forward to some of them. Agatha goes through Jen’s to-do list, as Rio hums and comments on a few. It doesn’t take long for Agatha to figure out that Alice means as much to Rio, as Jen does to her.

They discuss the upcoming bachelorette parties, (“ Why two? We could just hire one stripper and be done for the both of them?”) and decide it’s easier if both women take responsibility for their own friend’s party, not mingling with the plans for the other. They would have to be present for both, of course. The pre-wedding is something neither of them knows what it entails exactly, but they agree on figuring it out later.

Nearing the end of the phone call, Agatha feels a sense of relief that it hasn’t ended in national tragedy. She rubs her temple as Rio wraps up, lets out a breath she didn’t realize she was holding, and drops her arm back in the water with an audible slosh.

“...so for the most part, it will just be… uh– Are– you…– Agatha, are you taking a bath?” Rio stammers distractedly. Agatha squeezes her eyes shut, realizing her mistake, and silently curses herself. She is not gonna give Rio any mental images to have her way with.

“None of your business.” She sits up, proud of her thoughtful and eloquent response, but it only causes more sloshing. Rio’s shy giggle completely throws her off balance.

“Is the idea of talking to me that exciting?”

Oh, here we fucking go, Agatha thinks. “On the contrary.”

“Or did you start practicing for when we’re in a hot tub together?”

“Like I said, none of your fucking– wait, hot tub? What hot tub?”

“The one at the hotel. Where… the wedding takes place,” Rio says carefully, now realizing Agatha might not be up to date.

“Rio, I am so scared to ask you this,” she says, pinching the bridge of her nose, the lingering in Rio’s voice not lost on her, “but… what hotel? Where? Where is the wedding?”

She swears she hears Rio gulp before hearing her squeak: “Mexico?”




Which is, not coincidentally, the exact word Agatha screeches when she barges into Jen’s skin care boutique the next day. Jen barely acknowledges her and very calmly screws the lid on a bottle, only using index finger and thumb.

“You spoke to Rio, then?” She rests her elbows on the table and looks up at her friend who, in that moment, looks comically similar to Hades from the animated movie Hercules.

“You forgot to tell me the wedding I’m supposed to plan is going to be in fucking Mexico? Or did you think that’s just a minor detail? Or, were you going to publicly announce it again, like-”

“We decided last week. But, Agatha– what’s up with all this anger? I thought it’d be nice for you to have an excuse to take a few days off, chill out at the beach, bask in the sun-”

“Some of us have a job -”

“You run your own practice, Agatha-”

“And how am I supposed to plan everything when I don’t know-”

“You don’t have to do this alone, remember?”

“And maybe that’s the issue, on top of everything you’re making me do this with her -”

“Rio speaks Spanish-”

“And why did she know and I didn’t?”

“Ah, there it is,” Jen nods. “So that’s the real issue?”

Agatha crosses her arms and exhales like a riled up bull. “I just– I don’t like surprises.”

Jen stands up and walks to the little coffee counter in the corner of the boutique, placing two cups under the machine and pressing a button. “It wasn’t meant to be a surprise, Agatha,” she says over the loud noise of the coffee machine. “I told you– we decided last week, and Alice simply got to talk to Rio before I got to talk to you. That’s it.”

Agatha looks at her incredulously, but thaws out when Jen hands her a steaming cup. “I’d like for you to keep me in the loop next time,” she murmurs to her coffee.
She hates this feeling– when other people know something she doesn’t. And to go through that kind of embarrassment while Rio is on the other side of the phone is not something she wants to experience again. It makes her feel… stupid. Out of control. Powerless.

She sips her coffee and makes a face. “I keep forgetting the chemical waste you serve your clients as a sorry excuse for–”

Her right knee buckles. And when Rio pulls away, they spend the rest of the walk back pretending Rio hadn’t noticed that.

Chapter Notes

thank you for 1000+ kudos!!! speechless

The hot Mexican sun makes Agatha’s cheeks flush. She sits back on the lounger on the balcony of her hotel room, closes the lid of her sunscreen, and puts her sunglasses on.
It’s been two days since she, Jen, and Alice arrived here; and apart from dealing with her friends’ sickening smooching and generally being all lovey-dovey the entire time, it has been nothing but relaxing.

She’d put in some extra hours so that she could actually take two full weeks off without having to think about work or any errands she should be running. Now her biggest concern in the morning is which bathing suit to wear that day, and her biggest concern in the afternoon is whether it's time to reapply her sunscreen. She can definitely get used to this. Sure, there’s a wedding coming up–but there’s plenty of time to chill.

She crosses one leg and picks up her ereader from the side table. She smirks as she clicks it on and it shows her the page where she’d left off– it’s the lead up to a pretty spicy chapter.
This is a book Rio had recommended to her during one of their Zooms, and to her own surprise, she quite likes it. It’s actually been such a thoughtful move, she realizes, as this introduces her to some pretty detailed woman-on-woman intimacy without having to participate herself.

Rio had scoffed when Agatha had initially asked her why she wouldn’t just send her a link to her favorite lesbian porn video.
“You shouldn’t watch it, you should read it,” Rio had said. “You’d be surprised what happens when your own fantasy fills in the gaps.”

And so Agatha had downloaded her suggestion and started reading– reluctantly at first, but after just two chapters the sexual tension between the two women in the story got so intense, she hadn’t been able to put it down. This had almost gotten her into trouble when she’d read through the first sex scene while on the plane– tactically angling the screen away from Jen’s prying eyes. She had been able to imagine everything so vividly and when one of the characters in the book had started begging the other to please fuck her already, Agatha’s face had gotten bright red as she’d knitted her brows– her eyes almost rolling back in their sockets.
The steaminess of it had manifested as an uncomfortable flash of heat and so she’d turned it off to quickly take a few large gulps from her water bottle. Jen, upon noticing her discomfort, had slowly faced her to ask if everything was alright. Luckily she’d been able to save herself by shrugging it off, “just a hot flash,” and when Jen had asked her what book she was reading immediately after that, she’d been able to convince her it was an educational paper on the psychology behind aircraft safety procedures.

Nearing the end of the book now, she actually finds it quite exhilarating to read this in public. Nobody’s able to tell she’s reading an erotic novel– oh, who’s she kidding? It’s porn – so it feels like her own dirty little secret. And sometimes, the idea that Rio had read all of this too, adds a little extra something to the good parts.
As she’s approaching one of those good parts, she gets abruptly torn away from the story by a loud whistle from somewhere below her balcony. Ugh, had they picked an adult-only hotel for nothing?
Slightly irritated, she tries to focus back on the story, wherein one of the two women is very, very close to reaching an explosive orgasm–

Then, she hears the whistle again. Louder this time.
She throws her legs to the side and springs up from the lounger to glare down over the railing of the balcony. Her heart leaps – actually leaps – at the sight of a gleefully waving Rio.

“Hey hot stuff!” Rio yells up at her. Her right hand is still on the handle of her suitcase, and her left hand lands on the stylish sun hat on her head. She’s wearing sunglasses too, but they do nothing to hide the radiating smile on her face.
Agatha feels her entire body starting to buzz. It feels almost like she’s being tickled from the inside; it makes her grin. She pulls her own sunglasses down to the tip of her nose, looking down at Rio over the rim.

“Why the hell are you in sweatpants?” she shouts down. Rio looks down at her own body like she has no idea what she’s wearing.

“Oh come on, I literally just got off the plane!” she shouts back. “No need to start judging me already. I’m gonna check in and I’ll go change!”

“You better!”

Instead of walking, Rio keeps rooted in place. Agatha assumes she needs directions, so she points towards the reception. But Rio sets her suitcase straight up to open her arms wide.

“Well?” she calls out, wiggling her fingers. “Are you gonna come down or what, Juliet?”

Agatha laughs heartily– there’s a warm feeling in her stomach that spreads like a wildfire.

“I’m not sure that’s the correct line, Romeo!” she yells back with her hand curved around her mouth. “Gimme 30 seconds!”

She turns around, all but stumbles back into her room, rushing to her mirror to check herself out. Tugging on the hem of her sundress, she angles herself to check out her legs– yeah, she’s ready.
Before she leaves, she takes her sunglasses off her face and places them on top of her head, functioning like an elegant hair band. Snatching the key card from the nightstand, she exits the room and starts speed walking down the hall, until she realizes how ridiculous she looks and she forces herself down to a lazy strut. The elevator ride takes about three fucking business days to get down, but when the door opens, she already catches sight of Rio, patiently waiting in the entrance hall.
Rio notices her too, and raises her wrist to tap at a fake watch.

“That was at least two minutes, Agatha. Who do you think you are to keep me waiting?” she smirks. Agatha shakes her head, smiling, and walks towards her with her arms outstretched.

“Shut up, idiot. Come here.”

Not wanting to make their embrace uncomfortably long, Agatha pulls back relatively quickly– but Rio doesn’t let go yet. She would recognize this scent anywhere, as it’s so undoubtedly Rio– and yet, this time it does something different to her than the last time she’d smelled it.
